Below is a structured technical documentation of the system you have been building. Also, complete chat history of recent GPT communication This is written as if it were a project architecture document / technical brief, so it can also serve as reference material for future development, debugging, or portfolio documentation.
No code fixes are included here — the goal is clarity of the system you built, its architecture, and lessons learned.

1. Project Overview
Project Name
Open Claude Cowork – Autonomous AI Co-Worker System
Objective
To build a local AI-powered autonomous coworker capable of:
	•	Conversational interaction
	•	Task planning
	•	Executing tools
	•	Controlling browser actions
	•	Automating workflows
	•	Acting like a developer assistant or product builder
The system aims to emulate capabilities seen in:
	•	Devin
	•	OpenDevin
	•	Claude Code
	•	Cursor Agents
	•	Replit AI Agents

2. System Architecture
The system follows a layered architecture composed of multiple interacting components.
User Interface (Electron Desktop App)
        │
Renderer Layer (Chat + UI logic)
        │
Electron IPC Bridge
        │
Express Backend API
        │
Provider Layer
        │
Agent Runtime
        │
Tools / External APIs
        │
LLM Providers
Each layer has a distinct responsibility.

3. Core Components
3.1 Electron Desktop Client
The frontend application is built using Electron, which allows running a web-based interface as a desktop app.
Responsibilities
	•	Rendering the chat interface
	•	Streaming AI responses
	•	Displaying tool executions
	•	Showing planning steps
	•	Managing chat history
	•	Handling UI interactions
Key File
renderer/renderer.js
UI Features
	•	Chat window
	•	Chat history sidebar
	•	Tool call visualization
	•	Progress panel
	•	Live browser embedding
	•	Model selector
	•	Provider selector

3.2 Renderer Layer
The renderer acts as the presentation layer.
Responsibilities
	•	Sending user messages to backend
	•	Streaming response tokens
	•	Parsing SSE events
	•	Displaying tool calls inline
	•	Maintaining conversation state
Event Types Processed
Typical streaming events include:
connected
session_init
content
text
tool_use
tool_result
done
error

3.3 Electron IPC Bridge
Electron isolates frontend and backend processes.
Communication happens via IPC (Inter-Process Communication).
Responsibilities:
	•	Forward chat requests to backend
	•	Handle streaming responses
	•	Abort requests
	•	Control system tools

3.4 Backend API Server
The backend server is implemented using Node.js with Express.
Responsibilities
	•	Provide HTTP endpoints
	•	Manage streaming responses
	•	Route requests to providers
	•	Maintain chat sessions
	•	Handle tool execution
Server Endpoints
Health check:
GET /api/health
Chat endpoint:
POST /api/chat
Provider list:
GET /api/providers

3.5 Provider Layer
The provider layer abstracts the LLM model integrations.
It allows the system to switch between different AI providers.
Providers Supported
	•	Claude
	•	Opencode models
	•	OpenRouter models
	•	GLM models
Provider Files
server/providers/base-provider.js
server/providers/claude-provider.js
server/providers/opencode-provider.js
Responsibilities
	•	Create AI sessions
	•	Stream responses
	•	Manage chat context
	•	Trigger tool calls
	•	Handle abort signals

3.6 Agent Runtime
The system implements an agent-like execution model.
Instead of simply answering text prompts, the AI can:
	•	plan tasks
	•	execute tools
	•	observe results
	•	continue reasoning
This resembles the Plan → Execute → Observe → Repeat loop.

3.7 Tool System
The system supports external tools via Composio.
Tools allow the AI to interact with real-world systems.
Examples
Browser control
open website

navigate pages
File system actions
create file
edit file
read file
delete file
Terminal commands
run shell commands
execute scripts
install dependencies
Automation tasks
write todos
track progress
manage steps

4. Data Flow Architecture
When a user sends a message, the flow is:
User Prompt
     │

     │

     │

     │

     │

     │

     │

     │

5. Streaming Protocol
The system uses Server-Sent Events (SSE).
Example response stream:
data: {"type":"connected"}

data: {"type":"session_init"}

data: {"type":"content","content":"Hello"}

data: {"type":"tool_use"}

data: {"type":"tool_result"}

data: {"type":"done"}
The renderer continuously parses this stream.

6. Entity Relationship Model
The system operates around a few core entities.
Entities
User Chat Session Message Tool Call Tool Result
Relationship Diagram
User
 │
 └── ChatSession
        │
        ├── Message
        │
        └── ToolCall
                │
                └── ToolResult

7. Session Management
Each chat session has a unique identifier.
Example format:
chat_1773058171834_fmj91i9vz
Sessions allow:
	•	conversation memory
	•	tool tracking
	•	streaming continuity

8. Autonomous Workflow Model
The system attempts to support autonomous task execution.
Example workflow:
User request
Create a website
Agent plan
1 Generate HTML
2 Generate CSS
3 Create files
4 Start local server
5 Open browser
Each step triggers tools.

9. Browser Automation
One of the system’s most powerful capabilities is live browser control.
Features implemented:
	•	opening websites
	•	embedding live browser sessions
	•	sidebar browser view
	•	switching between inline and sidebar browser
Example use cases
open youtube
search google
open documentation
verify webpage output

10. Multi-Model Support
The UI allows switching between multiple models.
Examples include:
opencode/glm-4.7-free
opencode/gpt-5-nano
opencode/big-pickle
anthropic/claude-sonnet
anthropic/claude-opus

11. Project Design Philosophy
The design follows several principles.
Modular architecture
Each layer is separated.
Provider abstraction
Allows switching AI models.
Tool extensibility
New tools can be added easily.
Streaming interaction
Responses appear in real time.

12. Major Learning Outcomes
From the development process, several key insights emerged.
AI agents require stable infrastructure
Agent systems are far more complex than simple chatbots.
Streaming protocols must be consistent
Mismatch between backend event types and frontend parsing causes failures.
Provider abstraction is powerful but fragile
Supporting many providers increases flexibility but introduces complexity.
Tool systems introduce authentication dependencies
External tool frameworks often require API keys.

13. What Worked Successfully
During development, several features were confirmed working:
	•	streaming responses
	•	session management
	•	browser automation
	•	opening YouTube links
	•	executing tool calls
	•	displaying tool output in UI
	•	chat history persistence

14. What Did Not Work Consistently
Certain components caused instability.
Tool authentication
External tool systems failed due to invalid API keys.
Provider compatibility
Some models produced slightly different event formats.
Renderer parsing
Frontend expected different event types than backend emitted.
Configuration mismatch
Environment variables and provider settings caused runtime errors.

15. Current System State
From the logs provided, the system currently reaches:
Backend server running
Providers initialized
Chat request received
But tool initialization fails due to:
AuthenticationError
Invalid Composio API key
This stops tool routing from initializing.

16. Strategic Value of the Project
Despite instability during debugging, the project represents a significant build.
You effectively created a prototype of:
Local AI Operating System
Capabilities include:
	•	AI reasoning
	•	system control
	•	browser automation

This architecture is similar to emerging autonomous development agents.

17. Future Potential
If stabilized, the system could evolve into:
AI product builder
AI coding coworker

Automated workflow engine

18. Documentation Principle for Future Fixes
To avoid further instability, future debugging should follow strict rules.
Rule 1
Never change multiple core layers simultaneously.
Rule 2
Always commit working states.
Rule 3
Test layers individually.
Rule 4
Avoid guesswork in code changes.
Rule 5
Verify documentation and community discussions before modifying architecture.

19. Summary
This project represents an attempt to build a desktop autonomous AI coworker system combining:
	•	Electron UI
	•	Node.js backend
	•	AI provider abstraction
	•	tool execution
	•	browser automation
	•	streaming interaction
Although debugging introduced instability, the underlying architecture demonstrates the feasibility of such systems.
The most critical requirement moving forward is stability-first development, ensuring each component works independently before integrating the full agent pipeline.

# 7. Required Architecture for Agent Mode

To behave like Claude Code or OCC agent mode, the architecture must be:

User Task
↓
Planner
↓
Reasoning loop
↓
Tool selection
↓
Tool execution
↓
Observation
↓
Next step
↓
Completion


Agent loop structure:

while(task_not_complete):

   think()

   choose_tool()

   run_tool()

   observe_result()

   continue()

The Real Missing Layer
You correctly identified it:

OCC currently lacks an Agent Orchestrator
Right now your architecture is:

Prompt → LLM → text
But an autonomous coding agent requires:

Prompt
 ↓
Planner
 ↓
Reasoning Loop
 ↓
Tool Selection
 ↓
Tool Execution
 ↓
Observation
 ↓
Repeat
Without that loop, no autonomous work happens.

The 3 Missing Components
Your system is missing three critical modules.

1️⃣ Tool Schema Injection
The LLM must know what tools exist.

Example schema:

{
 "type": "function",
 "function": {
   "name": "read_file",
   "description": "Read contents of a file",
   "parameters": {
     "type": "object",
     "properties": {
       "path": { "type": "string" }
     },
     "required": ["path"]
   }
 }
}
These schemas must be sent in the OpenRouter request.

Example:

POST /chat/completions
{
  "model": "...",
  "messages": [...],
  "tools": [ ... ]
}
Without this, the model cannot call tools.

2️⃣ Tool Execution Handler
When the model responds:

tool_call
Your server must intercept it:

if (tool_call) {
   execute_tool()
   send_result_back()
}
Example event:

{
  type: "tool_call",
  tool: "FileRead",
  args: { path: "/Downloads/file.txt" }
}
3️⃣ Agent Reasoning Loop
You need the loop:

for step in max_steps:

   call_model()

   if tool_call:
       run_tool()

   if final_answer:
       break
This is the Claude Code architecture.

Correct Final OCC Architecture
Here is what OCC should become:

                ┌─────────────────────┐
                │   Electron UI       │
                │  (Renderer Agent)   │
                └──────────┬──────────┘
                           │
                           │ SSE
                           │
                ┌──────────▼──────────┐
                │ Node Server         │
                │ Express API         │
                └──────────┬──────────┘
                           │
                           │
                ┌──────────▼──────────┐
                │ Agent Orchestrator  │
                │ planner / executor  │
                └──────────┬──────────┘
                           │
                           │
                ┌──────────▼──────────┐
                │ LLM Provider        │
                │ OpenRouter / Claude │
                └──────────┬──────────┘

                           │ tool_calls
                           │

SESSION CONTEXT — OPEN CLAUDE COWORK RECOVERY

task: need to continue with the OCC agent fully autonomous , which is a tool-enabled version and which is a complete working agent loop version, complete continuity version until the job done, fully autonomous agent, completely agentic and orchestration version, like we would expect a OpenCloud co-worker to work end-to-end.

current opencode-provider.js -> import fetch from "node-fetch";

export class OpencodeProvider {

  constructor() {
    this.name = "opencode";
    this.apiKey = process.env.OPENROUTER_API_KEY;
    this.baseUrl = "https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions";
    this.abortControllers = new Map();
    this.sessions = new Map();
  }

  async initialize() {
    console.log("[Opencode] OpenRouter provider ready");
  }

  abort(chatId) {
    const controller = this.abortControllers.get(chatId);
    if (controller) {
      controller.abort();
      this.abortControllers.delete(chatId);
      return true;
    }
    return false;
  }

  async *query({ prompt, chatId }) {

    const abortController = new AbortController();
    this.abortControllers.set(chatId, abortController);

    try {

      const response = await fetch(this.baseUrl, {
        method: "POST",
        headers: {
          "Authorization": Bearer ${this.apiKey},
          "Content-Type": "application/json",
          "HTTP-Referer": "http://localhost",
          "X-Title": "Open-Claude-Cowork"
        },
        body: JSON.stringify({
          model: "openai/gpt-4o-mini",
          messages: [
            {
              role: "user",
              content: prompt
            }
          ],
          stream: true
        }),
        signal: abortController.signal
      });

      if (!response.ok) {

        const err = await response.text();

        yield {
          type: "text",
          content: OpenRouter error: ${err}
        };

        return;
      }

      let buffer = "";

      for await (const chunk of response.body) {

        buffer += chunk.toString();

        const lines = buffer.split("\n");
        buffer = lines.pop();

        for (const line of lines) {

          if (!line.startsWith("data:")) continue;

          const json = line.slice(5).trim();

          if (json === "[DONE]") return;

          try {

            const data = JSON.parse(json);
            const delta = data?.choices?.[0]?.delta?.content;

            if (delta) {

              yield {
                type: "text",
                content: delta
              };

            }

          } catch {}

        }

      }

    } catch (err) {

      yield {
        type: "text",
        content: "Provider error: " + err.message
      };

    } finally {

      this.abortControllers.delete(chatId);

    }

  }

}

server ->import express from 'express';
import cors from 'cors';
import path from 'path';
import { fileURLToPath } from 'url';
import fs from 'fs';
import dotenv from 'dotenv';
import { Composio } from '@composio/core';
import { getProvider, getAvailableProviders, initializeProviders } from './providers/index.js';

const __filename = fileURLToPath(import.meta.url);
const __dirname = path.dirname(__filename);

dotenv.config({ path: path.join(__dirname, '..', '.env') });

const app = express();
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 3001;

// Initialize Composio
const composio = new Composio();

const composioSessions = new Map();
let defaultComposioSession = null;

// Pre-initialize Composio session on startup
async function initializeComposioSession() {
  const defaultUserId = 'default-user';
  console.log('[COMPOSIO] Pre-initializing session for:', defaultUserId);
  try {
    defaultComposioSession = await composio.create(defaultUserId);
    composioSessions.set(defaultUserId, defaultComposioSession);
    console.log('[COMPOSIO] Session ready with MCP URL:', defaultComposioSession.mcp.url);

    // Update opencode.json with the MCP config
    updateOpencodeConfig(defaultComposioSession.mcp.url, defaultComposioSession.mcp.headers);
    console.log('[OPENCODE] Updated opencode.json with MCP config');
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('[COMPOSIO] Failed to pre-initialize session:', error.message);
  }
}

// Write MCP config to opencode.json
function updateOpencodeConfig(mcpUrl, mcpHeaders) {
  const opencodeConfigPath = path.join(__dirname, 'opencode.json');
  const config = {
    mcp: {
      composio: {
        type: 'remote',
        url: mcpUrl,
        headers: mcpHeaders
      }
    }
  };
  fs.writeFileSync(opencodeConfigPath, JSON.stringify(config, null, 2));
}

// Middleware
app.use(cors());
app.use(express.json());

// Chat endpoint using provider abstraction
app.post('/api/chat', async (req, res) => {
  const {
    message,
    chatId,
    userId = 'default-user',
    provider: providerName = 'claude',  // Per-request provider selection
    model = null  // Per-request model selection
  } = req.body;

  console.log('[CHAT] Request received:', message);
  console.log('[CHAT] Chat ID:', chatId);
  console.log('[CHAT] Provider:', providerName);
  console.log('[CHAT] Model:', model || '(default)');

  if (!message) {
    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Message is required' });
  }

  // Validate provider
  const availableProviders = getAvailableProviders();
  if (!availableProviders.includes(providerName.toLowerCase())) {
    return res.status(400).json({
      error: Invalid provider: ${providerName}. Available: ${availableProviders.join(', ')}
    });
  }

  res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'text/event-stream');
  res.setHeader('Cache-Control', 'no-cache, no-transform');
  res.setHeader('Connection', 'keep-alive');
  res.setHeader('X-Accel-Buffering', 'no');
  res.flushHeaders();

  res.write(data: ${JSON.stringify({ type: 'connected', message: 'Processing request...' })}\n\n);

  const heartbeatInterval = setInterval(() => {
    if (!res.writableEnded) {
      res.write(': heartbeat\n\n');
    }
  }, 15000);

  res.on('close', () => {
    clearInterval(heartbeatInterval);
  });

  try {
    // Get or create Composio session for this user
    let composioSession = composioSessions.get(userId);
    if (!composioSession) {
      console.log('[COMPOSIO] Creating new session for user:', userId);
      res.write(data: ${JSON.stringify({ type: 'status', message: 'Initializing session...' })}\n\n);
      composioSession = await composio.create(userId);
      composioSessions.set(userId, composioSession);
      console.log('[COMPOSIO] Session created with MCP URL:', composioSession.mcp.url);

      // Update opencode.json with the MCP config
      updateOpencodeConfig(composioSession.mcp.url, composioSession.mcp.headers);
      console.log('[OPENCODE] Updated opencode.json with MCP config');
    }

    // Get the provider instance
    const provider = getProvider(providerName);

    // Build MCP servers config - passed to provider
    const mcpServers = {
      composio: {
        type: 'http',
        url: composioSession.mcp.url,
        headers: composioSession.mcp.headers
      }
    };

    console.log('[CHAT] Using provider:', provider.name);
    console.log('[CHAT] All stored sessions:', Array.from(provider.sessions.entries()));

    // Stream responses from the provider
    try {
      for await (const chunk of provider.query({
        prompt: message,
        chatId,
        userId,
        mcpServers,
        model,
        allowedTools: ['Read', 'Write', 'Edit', 'Bash', 'Glob', 'Grep', 'WebSearch', 'WebFetch', 'TodoWrite', 'Skill'],
        maxTurns: 100
      })) {
        if (chunk.type === 'tool_use') {
          console.log('[SSE] Sending tool_use:', chunk.name);
        }
        if (chunk.type === 'text') {
          console.log('[SSE] Sending text chunk, length:', chunk.content?.length || 0);
        }
        // Send chunk as SSE
        const data = data: ${JSON.stringify(chunk)}\n\n;
        res.write(data);
      }
    } catch (streamError) {
      console.error('[CHAT] Stream error during iteration:', streamError);
      if (!res.writableEnded) {
        res.write(data: ${JSON.stringify({ type: 'error', message: streamError.message })}\n\n);
      }
    }

    clearInterval(heartbeatInterval);
    if (!res.writableEnded) {
      res.end();
    }
    console.log('[CHAT] Stream completed');
  } catch (error) {
    clearInterval(heartbeatInterval);
    console.error('[CHAT] Error:', error);
    res.write(data: ${JSON.stringify({ type: 'error', message: error.message })}\n\n);
    res.end();
  }
});

// Abort endpoint to stop active queries
app.post('/api/abort', (req, res) => {
  const { chatId, provider: providerName = 'claude' } = req.body;

  if (!chatId) {
    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'chatId is required' });
  }

  console.log('[ABORT] Request to abort chatId:', chatId, 'provider:', providerName);

  try {
    const provider = getProvider(providerName);
    const aborted = provider.abort(chatId);

    if (aborted) {
      console.log('[ABORT] Successfully aborted chatId:', chatId);
      res.json({ success: true, message: 'Query aborted' });
    } else {
      console.log('[ABORT] No active query found for chatId:', chatId);
      res.json({ success: false, message: 'No active query to abort' });
    }
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('[ABORT] Error:', error);
    res.status(500).json({ error: error.message });
  }
});

// Get available providers endpoint
app.get('/api/providers', (_req, res) => {
  res.json({
    providers: getAvailableProviders(),
    default: 'claude'
  });
});

// Health check endpoint
app.get('/api/health', (_req, res) => {
  res.json({
    status: 'ok',
    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),
    providers: getAvailableProviders()
  });
});

await initializeProviders();
await initializeComposioSession();

// Start server and keep reference to prevent garbage collection
const server = app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(\n✓ Backend server running on http://localhost:${PORT});
  console.log(✓ Chat endpoint: POST http://localhost:${PORT}/api/chat);
  console.log(✓ Providers endpoint: GET http://localhost:${PORT}/api/providers);
  console.log(✓ Health check: GET http://localhost:${PORT}/api/health);
  console.log(✓ Available providers: ${getAvailableProviders().join(', ')}\n);
});

// Keep the process alive
server.on('error', (err) => {
  console.error('Server error:', err);
});

// Prevent the process from exiting
process.on('SIGINT', () => {
  console.log('\nShutting down server...');
  server.close(() => {
    console.log('Server closed');
    process.exit(0);
  });
});


renderer -> // DOM Elements - Views
const homeView = document.getElementById('homeView');

// State
let isFirstMessage = true;
let todos = [];
let toolCalls = [];
let attachedFiles = [];
let selectedProvider = 'claude';
let selectedModel = 'claude-sonnet-4-5-20250514';
let thinkingMode = 'normal'; // 'normal' or 'extended'
let isWaitingForResponse = false;

let activeBrowserSession = null; // { url: string, sessionId: string, inlineElement: HTMLElement }
let browserDisplayMode = 'hidden'; // 'inline' | 'sidebar' | 'hidden'

// Multi-chat state
let allChats = [];
let currentChatId = null;

// Model configurations per provider
const providerModels = {
